<div id="review_315224694" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/315224694" />
    <a title="Aoibhínn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5799885-aoibh-nn"><img alt="Aoibhínn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452957222p2/5799885.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/315224694?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aoibhínn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aoibhínn" href="/user/show/5799885-aoibh-nn">Aoibhínn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780857076076" href="/book/show/12317877-the-future-of-us">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer315224694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10726158922503043397">The narrators of the novel are 16-year-olds, Emma and Josh, who live next door to each other and have been best friends for as long as they can remember. One day Emma is given a computer and an AOL CD-Rom with 100 free hours on it. Emma goes online and finds her Facebook page from 15 years into the future!<br/><br/>This novel was a nostalgia trip back to 1996 for me – when the Internet was brand spanking new and we all had to connect to it with painfully slow (and incredibly noisy) dial up, when we all li</span>
  <span id="freeText10726158922503043397" style="display:none">The narrators of the novel are 16-year-olds, Emma and Josh, who live next door to each other and have been best friends for as long as they can remember. One day Emma is given a computer and an AOL CD-Rom with 100 free hours on it. Emma goes online and finds her Facebook page from 15 years into the future!<br /><br />This novel was a nostalgia trip back to 1996 for me – when the Internet was brand spanking new and we all had to connect to it with painfully slow (and incredibly noisy) dial up, when we all listened to music on our Discmans and no one knew what an mp3 was, and when no one had mobile phones apart from the very rich. I was 15 years old in 1996 so this novel provided me with great memories of the 90's and it made me think about how much technology has changed and now much it has affected our lives. <br /><br />The Future of Us is an interesting, entertaining and enjoyable read. Both the characters and the unique plot were very well developed. It's really about a journey of self-discovery and seizing the moment. Three and a half stars! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10726158922503043397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_181750264" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/181750264" />
    <a title="Isamlq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq"><img alt="Isamlq" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483590305p2/4016030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/181750264?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer181750264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17213507772394084511">I’m recalling some pretty <s>interesting</s> funny things care of my family. The nineties as history?! There was my brother and his love for Wayne’s World, and low slung jeans puffy sweaters. My sister and her love of the group soul ballad. Boyz 2 Men, it mentions, but my sister was all about All Saints. And later still there was her fondness for the Backstreet Boys and their Quit Playing with-what’s it. I, on the other hand, had Captain Planet and Gem to focus on (wait, it will come back to you.) So i</span>
  <span id="freeText17213507772394084511" style="display:none">I’m recalling some pretty <s>interesting</s> funny things care of my family. The nineties as history?! There was my brother and his love for Wayne’s World, and low slung jeans puffy sweaters. My sister and her love of the group soul ballad. Boyz 2 Men, it mentions, but my sister was all about All Saints. And later still there was her fondness for the Backstreet Boys and their Quit Playing with-what’s it. I, on the other hand, had Captain Planet and Gem to focus on (wait, it will come back to you.) So in 1996 all I’m remembering is Saturday morning cartoons. And that Cricket doll (with a creepy resemblance to Chucky, the doll possessed by that psycho soul.) Why do I find it funny that it’s a time is marked by what people found popular? I feel a little like the nineties is too recent a past to be looked upon like it is the Past with a capital P, as in capable of being the subject of something so vague as in time travel, but hey.. .why not?<br /><br />All that said, I thought the concept of this one quirky if not as well executed as say READY PLAYER ONE (Read that one now ). Emma gets a PC and logs on to the facebook fifteen years in the future. Isn’t there a danger of it becoming dated? Right now it’s quirky reading how someone in the past reads something so commonly occurring, but give it a few years, and THE FUTURE OF US will likely read odd. But that’s the point, right? <br /><br />That aside, the people in the story are nothing new. I enjoyed Josh more than I did Emma. For one, she could be so insensitive and self involved. Josh on the other hand is pretty ordinary. Their reactions to the same thing emphasized these aspects of them. I’d have loved to see more of Tyson, especially how easy and jokey he could be. <br /><br />So, they have a history and when one screwed up and so did the other; there’s really not that much to it. 1996 as history and facebook as the future are about all that’s different here. <br />Moving on.<br /><br /><b>2.5/5<br />PBT #3</b><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17213507772394084511" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_222336068" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/222336068" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/222336068?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer222336068" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11698338116590268014">Fun, fun, fun!<br/>Cute, cute, cute!<br/><br/><b>The Future of Us</b> has a really neat time travel concept that people should get a real kick out of, specially if you have facebook. This was pretty creative and so much fun that I lost myself completely, reading this in just a span of a few hours. Unputdownable.<br/><br/>Josh and Emma are so adorable. Life long friends who drifted apart since one wanted more then the other, but when Emma gets her first computer and Josh brings over AOL things are put into motion that neither o</span>
  <span id="freeText11698338116590268014" style="display:none">Fun, fun, fun!<br />Cute, cute, cute!<br /><br /><b>The Future of Us</b> has a really neat time travel concept that people should get a real kick out of, specially if you have facebook. This was pretty creative and so much fun that I lost myself completely, reading this in just a span of a few hours. Unputdownable.<br /><br />Josh and Emma are so adorable. Life long friends who drifted apart since one wanted more then the other, but when Emma gets her first computer and Josh brings over AOL things are put into motion that neither of them would have ever expected.<br />I love time travel books, and while I'm not sure this is considered one in the more traditional sense, I'm still calling it that since Josh and Emma get snip-its of what their lives will be like fifteen years from now.<br /><br />I loved Josh and thought he was just a great, kind and sweet person. I loved how he acted like a guy once he found out who he was marrying. So cute!! Emma was a good character as well, but she was very frustrating. She became obsessed and mean about her future. She does't know what she wants and doesn't seem like a very happy person. This one thing she did to Josh was a pretty low-blow and I was annoyed that she never even said sorry, but I liked what she tried to do for her best friend and she turned out to be better as the story went on.<br />The only thing I really didn't care for were Josh's parents. They kinda were just there and I didn't find them necessary to the story-line.<br /><br />Bottom line, this was a really fun experience and it was the perfect book after reading something heavy like Froi. It was light and easy and simply a really sweet read!<br /><br />Thanks Arlene for sending it out and Alexa for sharing this one. <br />I had a blast reading this!:)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11698338116590268014" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_216244769" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/216244769" />
    <a title="Maria " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5769334-maria"><img alt="Maria " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600318539p2/5769334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/216244769?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria " href="/user/show/5769334-maria">Maria </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer216244769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer597811882505587793">If there was a device or a program that would let you give a preview of what your life would be 15 years from now, would you try it out?<br/>Would you really like to know how life has turned out for you and the people around you?<br/>When you find out that your life after 15 years sucks, would you try and change it in your present time?<br/><br/>Josh's mom told him to bring the AOL CD they received to Emma's place because she recently received her new PC.<br/>They installed it.<br/>Emma made her email address and then a myst</span>
  <span id="freeText597811882505587793" style="display:none">If there was a device or a program that would let you give a preview of what your life would be 15 years from now, would you try it out?<br />Would you really like to know how life has turned out for you and the people around you?<br />When you find out that your life after 15 years sucks, would you try and change it in your present time?<br /><br />Josh's mom told him to bring the AOL CD they received to Emma's place because she recently received her new PC.<br />They installed it.<br />Emma made her email address and then a mysterious website appeared.<br />It was Facebook.<br />But Facebook has not yet been invented in 1996.<br />What did they find in Facebook?<br />They found themselves looking at themselves fifteen years in the future.<br /><br />After Thirteen Reasons Why, I was an immediate Jay Asher fan.<br />Anything that would have his name on it, I would definitely read.<br />That was one reason I opened this book which by the way I didn’t regret.<br /><br />The concept of The Future of Us was creative.<br />Who would think of creating a story with Facebook in it but set fifteen years before it was even invented.<br />It was cool.<br />It was genius.<br />The writing style was great as usual.<br />The book was told in alternating POV's of Emma and Josh which really did the job.<br />It made me see both sides of the main characters.<br />It was original.<br />The feel of the book was really 90ish.<br />Discmans.<br />Dial-ups.<br />Dave Matthews.<br />It gave me a little bit of nostalgia.<br />No doubt the story was well thought of.<br />I have some issues with the characters though.<br /><br />Let me start with Emma.<br />I hate Emma.<br />She was just so shallow for me.<br />She was so unlikable.<br />There was nothing about her that I liked.<br />If I was given the chance to look at myself 15 years from now, I wouldn’t obsess over who would be the person I get married to.<br />She was so unhappy that when she finds out that Josh was married to someone pretty, popular and rich while her future self was struggling with her marriage.<br />*Sigh*<br />She doesn’t know how to love anyone.<br />Her relationship with her exes? Not good!<br />She sucks.<br />Honestly, I hope Sydney ended up with Josh.<br />She didn’t deserve him at all!<br />Selfish little b*tch!<br /><br />Although, I dislike Emma, I liked Josh.<br />He was nice and sweet.<br />He wasn’t the type of guy Emma would go for because he was decent.<br />Skanky Emma goes for the ones who like to take advantage of a girl. (ex. Cody)<br />Josh deserved better.<br />He deserved the future that he was supposed to have because he was decent.<br />No girl in the right mind would turn him down the way Emma did.<br />*Stupid, stupid EMMA!*<br />Josh was genuine.<br />I love Josh's character but there were some point in the book that I thought he was becoming like Emma.<br />He got a little obsessed with the future thing about him and Sydney that he acted stupid.<br />But he redeemed himself which I was really proud of.<br /><br />I liked Kellan and Tyson.<br />Emma looked at Kellan's Facebook page but why not Tyson's?<br />She would have known the answer to her question about Kellan if she did.<br /><br />Although I hate Emma for being who she is, I couldn’t blame her for obsessing over what happened to her in the future.<br />She focused a lot on his husband sure but still she wanted to make things right in her future.<br />I probably would have done the same if I was in her shoes.<br />But I think that was the moral lesson of this book, "We should let things take its course."<br />No matter how much we blame other people for what happens to us in the end we are all responsible for our actions.<br /><br />The Future of Us was a very quick read.<br />It was fast-paced.<br />Jay Asher, you did it again.<br /><br />I would give this a 4.<br />Maybe if Emma was a bit like Sydney, I would have liked her.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="597811882505587793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240156874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12173337021676289047">I didn't like <a href='http://bookchilla.wordpress.com/2011/12/06/book-review-the-future-of-us-by-jay-asher-carolyn-mackler/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Future of Us</a>.<br/><br/>*****<br/><br/><b>PLAIN.</b><br/><br/><i>The Future of Us</i> was a flop for me. I thought the “Facebook” theme would evolve into something more meaningful than it actually is, but it did not. The writing was unimpressive; the female lead was irritating; the love story is kinda all over the place. I hope you are not pining for The Future of Us because it is not worth waiting for.<br/> <br/><b>Emma</b> is obnoxious to Josh. She’s selfish and self-centered. I could not find a single thing to like about her! Although </span>
  <span id="freeText12173337021676289047" style="display:none">I didn't like <a href="http://bookchilla.wordpress.com/2011/12/06/book-review-the-future-of-us-by-jay-asher-carolyn-mackler/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Future of Us</a>.<br /><br />*****<br /><br /><b>PLAIN.</b><br /><br /><i>The Future of Us</i> was a flop for me. I thought the “Facebook” theme would evolve into something more meaningful than it actually is, but it did not. The writing was unimpressive; the female lead was irritating; the love story is kinda all over the place. I hope you are not pining for The Future of Us because it is not worth waiting for.<br /> <br /><b>Emma</b> is obnoxious to Josh. She’s selfish and self-centered. I could not find a single thing to like about her! Although she did learned with the Facebook fiasco, her character was underdeveloped for me. <b>Josh</b> – Josh is the sole reason why this book has any stars at all. He knows he’s a wallflower but still he goes for the hottest girl in school. He’s honest to his feelings and he confronted his ‘go-with-the-flow’ attitude. Frankly, Emma doesn’t deserve even a glance from Josh. But hey, at least Josh called out Emma on her callousness with his feelings. Right on, man!<br /> <br /><i>The Future of Us</i> is a passable read, meaning you can pass/skip reading this. I read nothing from Mackler; I read 13RW from Asher but I did not detect his writing style and impact in this book.</span>

<div id="review_2738255155" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2738255155" />
    <a title="Jay G" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30890847-jay-g"><img alt="Jay G" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505302632p2/30890847.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

  <span id="freeText1288328588556840029" style="display:none">Want to see more bookish things from me? check out my youtube channel: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCferU-BCL2dlFjWdD0rS75Q">https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCfer...</a><br /><br />In 1996, Emma and Josh are neighbours. They used to be very close but something happened between them that have caused them to drift apart. Josh receives an AOL CD which he brings over to Emma's one day when she gets a new computer. Once downloaded on the computer, a website called Facebook pops up and allows them to see 15 years into their futures. Every time they refresh the page, their futures change based off of things they do that day. <br /><br />I initially thought the concept of this book sounded so cool, but as I began reading I realized I didn't enjoy the writing style. I found the whole thing to be rather predictable and I wasn't very invested in either character or what happened to them. Emma was extremely selfish and she just made me angry for most of the book. Josh was a bit more likeable, but I still can't say I actually cared for him. </span>

<div id="review_243391153" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/243391153" />
    <a title="Annalisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/542037-annalisa"><img alt="Annalisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1226336540p2/542037.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/243391153?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annalisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annalisa" href="/user/show/542037-annalisa">Annalisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer243391153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15242018103091833916">This was a cute story. The book's a little simplistic (the 16-point font didn't help), nothing groundbreaking or amazing, but it was still enjoyable. I'd recommend it not only for teenagers but for those who were teenagers in the mid '90s. It was fun to go back and realize how different life was, how much we take for granted now. Getting off the Internet to use the phone, waiting for film to the develop, trips to the video store. Good times. Good times.<br/><br/>My main issue with the book was I struggled</span>
  <span id="freeText15242018103091833916" style="display:none">This was a cute story. The book's a little simplistic (the 16-point font didn't help), nothing groundbreaking or amazing, but it was still enjoyable. I'd recommend it not only for teenagers but for those who were teenagers in the mid '90s. It was fun to go back and realize how different life was, how much we take for granted now. Getting off the Internet to use the phone, waiting for film to the develop, trips to the video store. Good times. Good times.<br /><br />My main issue with the book was I struggled liking Emma. She complained about everything, liked the wrong guys for the wrong reasons, and took those who were good to her for granted. When she wondered why everyone in the future seemed happy but her, I thought she was finally learning a valuable lesson, but she missed it. Her friends in the future were happy because they chose to be, despite their circumstances, not because their lives were better than hers, which in some cases weren't. Learning that your decisions now affect the future was an important lesson, but so is the realization that you affect your happiness as much, if not more, than your circumstances. I wish Emma had learned that lesson. It would have made the ending stronger.<br /><br />Speaking of what made Emma unhappy, I could have had some of those points driven home more. Instead of her assuming she was unhappy from a few vague Facebook statuses <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[about her possibly giving up her career for her husband <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I would have liked that to be shown to me. Instead of making Emma sound whiny, I would have agreed and sympathized with her. It would have, once again, made the ending stronger.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I knew the book was headed toward its ending, but I wasn't convinced. I liked Josh with Sydney. Emma sounded like the shallow one, not Sydney. And I liked Emma with Kevin. I wasn't convinced that was a bad scenario either. Josh and Emma together was the logical ending, but I could have used more chemistry between them, more synching as only best-friends-for-life have, or, most importantly, more convincing that Emma was the right girl for Josh, not just Josh the right guy for Emma. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Despite my issues, the coauthoring worked well here. Mackler and Asher's writing styles complimented each other so that the characters had distinct voices but not the writing. Despite the fact that I have yet to give a Jay Asher book more than 3 stars, I like him. When he comes out with another book, I'll probably read it and if he ever shows up for an author signing nearby, I'll probably go. This was my first experience with Carolyn Mackler and would not be opposed to reading her again (I have one of her books on my to-read list). I'm off to Facebook. Please tell me my status updates aren't as shallow as these.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15242018103091833916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12335308579521947562">Eh, it was okay.<br/><br/><i>The Future of Us</i> had so much potential. I mean, the synopsis was great and really intrigued me. Yet, after diving into it.. I was bound to get annoyed quite easily. In it, you will meet Josh and Emma. They were best friends up to a certain point and that's about it.<br/><br/>Ha, just kidding. They are somehow reunited once again. I mean, yeah it's a complete mystery as to why two kids, who just happen to be neighbors, start talking and hanging out again. So weird. Well, they start to bond </span>
  <span id="freeText12335308579521947562" style="display:none">Eh, it was okay.<br /><br /><i>The Future of Us</i> had so much potential. I mean, the synopsis was great and really intrigued me. Yet, after diving into it.. I was bound to get annoyed quite easily. In it, you will meet Josh and Emma. They were best friends up to a certain point and that's about it.<br /><br />Ha, just kidding. They are somehow reunited once again. I mean, yeah it's a complete mystery as to why two kids, who just happen to be neighbors, start talking and hanging out again. So weird. Well, they start to bond over AOL. Ah, AOL - such a nice trip down memory lane.<br /><br />While being on the mystical and mysterious AOL, the are able to see tiny glimpses into their future. Why? Well, Facebook and a ton of other stuff that we use today aren't invented yet. So they are extremely baffled by what Facebook is. Yet, Emma is just so freaking obsessed with her future. She wants to know what her husband does, what she does, will she be rich, and all that jazz. Then there's Josh who doesn't truly believe who he ends up marrying but is overall happy with what he sees.<br /><br />Long story short, lots of drama happens and Emma just becomes more and more annoying with each page. Not sure what Josh sees in her.. but love is blind I guess. In the end, I was more than happy to talk away from this book.</span>

<div id="review_242877829" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/242877829" />
    <a title="Taneika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5591031-taneika"><img alt="Taneika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564410672p2/5591031.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/242877829?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taneika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taneika" href="/user/show/5591031-taneika">Taneika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780857076076" href="/book/show/12317877-the-future-of-us">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer242877829" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10904971392307229769">What would you do if you had your future at your fingertips? What would you have done if you stumbled upon Facebook 8 years before it was invented and you saw how your living in the future?<br/><br/>Josh and Emma have been best friends almost their entire lives until things get a little awkward... Josh gets a free AOL CD in the mail and gives it to Emma to install on her new computer. The pair then stumbles upon a website called Facebook and it's a little bit weird... Who would write about what their havi</span>
  <span id="freeText10904971392307229769" style="display:none">What would you do if you had your future at your fingertips? What would you have done if you stumbled upon Facebook 8 years before it was invented and you saw how your living in the future?<br><br>Josh and Emma have been best friends almost their entire lives until things get a little awkward... Josh gets a free AOL CD in the mail and gives it to Emma to install on her new computer. The pair then stumbles upon a website called Facebook and it's a little bit weird... Who would write about what their having for dinner or what colour they want to dye their hair? They have no idea how they came across Facebook when it hadn't even been invented yet or why their posting such personal things for everybody to see! <br><br>Whist I wasn't a teenager in the 90's, I still consider myself a 90's kid (is that something I should be proud of?). All the little bits and pieces mentioned such as scrunchies, dial up, Windows 95 (I refused to have any screensaver but the brick maze) and the fact that a COLOUR monitor was pretty freaking cool made me feel all giddy inside and I constantly found myself going "OOOOH I REMEMBER THAT!". Then there are the mentions of things we didn't have any idea about back then... For example,<br><i>'I flinch. "What the hell happens to Pluto?"'</i><br>or<br><i>'"It doesn't matter," Tyson says, biting off more sandwich. "My dad thinks Ellen DeGeneres is gay, and we love Ellen!"<br>"Are you kidding? She's not gay," Kellan says.'</i><br>and finally<br><i>'I don't know what Harry Potter or The Help are...</i><br><br>This is set before Harry Potter was a phenomenon (there was such a time? Must have blocked it out :P). The 90's nostalgia was great :)<br><br>This was written in dual narrative and I thought both character's had very distinctive voices and I really loved seeing them mature and grow throughout the novel. We still witness the freakouts either has over something they've seen on Facebook, but I found that the two of them handled situations very differently. I'm not entirely sure whether I liked Emma or not. I liked her, however she was never happy with what her future offered her and jumped to conclusions very easily. If it was implied that she had a bad week on Facebook, she would go to drastic measures to manipulate her future. She did this several times and whilst Josh understandably freaked out about a few things, he didn't do anything too drastic in attempt to change his future. Josh thought more rationally than Emma did and was a little more accepting. He didn't intentionally do anything to change his future, although he did "accidently" due to the simple fact he knew what would happen to him in 15 years.<br><br>Although the ending and the story in general fairly predictable, it was still a delightful, fun read and is a thought-provoking novel with just enough 90's nostalgia tossed in (which obviously, I really enjoyed!). Also, the ending is super-duper cute :)<br><br><a href="http://s1106.photobucket.com/albums/h365/TaneikaSm/?action=view&amp;current=MAZE95.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364291i/715933.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Ohhh yeahhh! <br><br>Also, did anyone else used to play <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chip%27s_Challenge" rel="nofollow noopener">Chip's Challenge</a>? Or was that just me :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10904971392307229769" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer261469006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2834708449327136738">For me this book is just okay. It had a really interesting concept. A high school girl in 1996 sets up her computer then sets up AOL. For reasons (unexplained still at the end of the novel) she finds Facebook already in her favorites. When she logs on she finds the her own profile 15 years in the future.<br/><br/>She looks at her future on Facebook and bemoans that she's not happy. So she tries to change her future. And it works! Her new future seems better than her first future, but she's still not satis</span>
  <span id="freeText2834708449327136738" style="display:none">For me this book is just okay. It had a really interesting concept. A high school girl in 1996 sets up her computer then sets up AOL. For reasons (unexplained still at the end of the novel) she finds Facebook already in her favorites. When she logs on she finds the her own profile 15 years in the future.<br /><br />She looks at her future on Facebook and bemoans that she's not happy. So she tries to change her future. And it works! Her new future seems better than her first future, but she's still not satisfied and tries to change it again. For me this was frustrating to read. Emma did not seem to understand that maybe the problem wasn't the men that she eventually married, but the problem was her. <br /><br />I could already tell what kind of facebooker Future Emma was. I'm sure you've all met this type before. The "My Life is So Bad Please Pity Me," facebooker. Unfortunately, I know a lot of these people. Sometimes I've even asked Facebook to only show me their "important updates" because the whining gets out of control. They're almost as bad as the overly religious Facebook posts that are my personal pet peeve (this week I'm downright angry over one that said "Share if you love God. If you Love the Devil Keep Scrolling).<br /><br />My main issue with this novel is Emma. I just didn't like her. She is a believable 16-year-old, but that's not always a good thing. She is so selfish throughout this book. She doesn't care who her decisions effect. With Emma it's all about her happiness. For me she crossed the line when she tried to change Kellen's future without her consent (even though Kellen looked happy in the future). <br /><br />1996 Emma is discontent and whiney. Her life isn't perfect but nobody's is. By the end of the book I'm not even sure that she understands that the problem isn't the men in her life, the problem is her perspective on life. There's a glimmer of hope, but she still seems to base her future potential happiness on the boys in her life. <br /><br />The book ends with future Emma deleting her facebook account. Emma philosophizes that maybe future Emma is somehow tuned into what past Emma is feeling. Say what? Shouldn't Future Emma remember Present Emma? That seemed to be a huge logic fail. If the ripples of Present Emma's choices effect her future, then how could her future self not remember discovering Facebook in 1996? And if Future Emma didn't remember then how did Present Emma have such an impact on her life? <br /><br />Time travel is always tricky. This book doesn't attempt to go into the science behind it (thank goodness) and completely ignores most of the conundrums it presents. If you're going to write a book about seeing the future these details need to be included. Ignoring them feels lazy.<br /><br />The book is a thoughtful look at how even the smallest choices impact the future. It just needed a more likable main character and more thought put into the implications of time travel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2834708449327136738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('t6NZSQNHGo533Aa8o1Iff6r0gE3Mz6L3Kp33RH/UopQrGT6MT5TJl6rQAjH4KPxMGtSOL4pzKnONQjKaj9PZ2g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/569269.Jay_Asher">About Jay Asher</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1315548341330237845">Jay Asher was born in Arcadia, California on September 30, 1975. He grew up in a family that encouraged all of his interests, from playing the guitar to his writing. He attended Cuesta College right after graduating from high school. It was here where he wrote his first two children’s books for a class called Children’s Literature Appreciation. At this point in his life, he had decided he wanted t</span>
  <span id="freeText1315548341330237845" style="display:none">Jay Asher was born in Arcadia, California on September 30, 1975. He grew up in a family that encouraged all of his interests, from playing the guitar to his writing. He attended Cuesta College right after graduating from high school. It was here where he wrote his first two children’s books for a class called Children’s Literature Appreciation. At this point in his life, he had decided he wanted to become an elementary school teacher. He then transferred to California Polytechnic State University in San Luis Obispo where he left his senior year in order to pursue his career as a serious writer. Throughout his life he worked in various establishments, including as a salesman in a shoe store and in libraries and bookstores. Many of his work experiences had an impact on some aspect of his writing.<br /><br />He has published only one book to date, <i>Thirteen Reasons Why</i>, which was published in October 2007. He is currently working on his second Young Adult novel, and has written several picture books and screenplays. <i>Thirteen Reasons Why</i> has won several awards and has received five stars from Teen Book Review. It also has received high reviews from fellow authors such as Ellen Hopkins, Chris Crutcher, and Gordon Kormon.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1315548341330237845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
